					<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading mw-first-heading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Metadata</span></h1>
							
<div id="p-lang-btn" class="vector-dropdown mw-portlet mw-portlet-lang"  >
	<input type="checkbox" id="p-lang-btn-checkbox" role="button" aria-haspopup="true" data-event-name="ui.dropdown-p-lang-btn" class="vector-dropdown-checkbox mw-interlanguage-selector" aria-label="Go to an article in another language. Available in 57 languages"   >
	<label id="p-lang-btn-label" for="p-lang-btn-checkbox" class="vector-dropdown-label cdx-button cdx-button--fake-button cdx-button--fake-button--enabled cdx-button--weight-quiet cdx-button--action-progressive mw-portlet-lang-heading-57" aria-hidden="true"  ><span class="vector-icon mw-ui-icon-language-progressive mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-language-progressive"></span>

<span class="vector-dropdown-label-text">57 languages</span>
	</label>
	<div class="vector-dropdown-content">

		<div class="vector-menu-content">
			
			<ul class="vector-menu-content-list">

					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-subjectpageheader">
</div><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Data about other data</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1305433154">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em ambox-lead&#95;too&#95;short" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/120px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="44" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article's <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Lead_section#Length" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Lead section">lead section</a> <b>may be too short to adequately <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Summary_style" title="Wikipedia:Summary style">summarize</a> the key points</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please consider expanding the lead to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Lead_section#Provide_an_accessible_overview" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Lead section">provide an accessible overview</a> of all important aspects of the article.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2025</span>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Schlagwortkatalog.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Schlagwortkatalog.jpg/250px-Schlagwortkatalog.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="211" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Schlagwortkatalog.jpg/500px-Schlagwortkatalog.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2128" data-file-height="1800" /></a><figcaption>In the 21st century, metadata typically refers to digital forms, but traditional card catalogs contain metadata, with cards holding <a href="/wiki/Information" title="Information">information</a> about books in a library (author, title, subject, etc.).</figcaption></figure>
<p><b>Metadata</b> (or <b>metainformation</b>) is <a href="/wiki/Data" title="Data">data</a> that defines and describes the characteristics of other data.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  It often helps to describe, explain, locate, or otherwise make data easier to retrieve, use, or manage. For example, the title, author, and publication date of a book are metadata about the book. But, while a data asset is finite, its metadata is infinite.
</p><p>As such, efforts to <a href="#Definition">define</a>, classify <a href="#Types">types</a>, or <a href="#Structure">structure</a> metadata are expressed as examples in the context of its <a href="#Use">use</a>. The term "metadata" has a <a href="#History">history</a> dating to the 1960s where it occurred in computer science and in <a href="#Popular_culture">popular culture</a>. Different types of metadata serve different functions. For example, descriptive metadata for a document might include the author, creation date, <a href="/wiki/File_size" title="File size">file size</a> and <a href="/wiki/Search_engine_optimization" title="Search engine optimization">keywords</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Types">Types</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Types"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>There are many distinct types of metadata, including:
</p>
<ul><li><b>Descriptive metadata</b> – the descriptive information about a resource. It is used for discovery and identification. It includes elements such as title, abstract, author, and keywords.</li>
<li><b>Structural metadata</b> – metadata about containers of data and indicates how compound objects are put together, for example, how pages are ordered to form chapters. It describes the types, versions, relationships, and other characteristics of digital materials.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>Administrative metadata</b><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Metadata&#95;Basics&#95;Outline&#95;3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metadata_Basics_Outline-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> – the information to help manage a resource, like resource type, and permissions, and when and how it was created.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Understanding&#95;Metadata&#95;(2)&#95;4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Understanding_Metadata_(2)-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>Reference metadata</b> – the information about the contents and quality of <a href="/wiki/Statistical_data_type" title="Statistical data type">statistical data</a>.</li>
<li><b>Statistical metadata</b><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:4&#95;5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> – also called process data, may describe processes that collect, process, or produce statistical data.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:5&#95;6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>Legal metadata</b> – provides information about the creator, <a href="/wiki/Copyright" title="Copyright">copyright</a> holder, and public licensing, if provided.</li></ul>
<p>Metadata is not strictly bound to one of these categories, as it can describe a piece of data in many other ways.
</p><p>While the metadata application is manifold, covering a large variety of fields, there are specialized and well-accepted models to specify types of metadata. <a href="/wiki/Francis_Bretherton" title="Francis Bretherton">Bretherton</a> &amp; Singley (1994) distinguish between two distinct classes: structural/control metadata and guide metadata.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i>Structural metadata</i> describes the structure of database objects such as tables, columns, keys and indexes. <i>Guide metadata</i> helps humans find specific items and is usually expressed as a set of keywords in a natural language. According to <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Kimball" title="Ralph Kimball">Ralph Kimball</a>, metadata can be divided into three categories: <i>technical metadata</i> (or internal metadata), <i>business metadata</i> (or external metadata), and <i>process metadata</i>. <a href="/wiki/Dan_Linstedt" title="Dan Linstedt">Dan Linstedt</a>, creator of the <a href="/wiki/Data_vault_modeling" title="Data vault modeling">data vault</a> methodology, says business metadata "...provide[s] definition of the functionality, definition of the data, definition of the elements, and definition of how the data is used within business...business metadata includes business requirements, time-lines, business metrics, business process flows, and business terminology."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Business metadata is important because it can greatly facilitate the usefulness of the data to business people.  A simple example of business metadata is a glossary entry.  Hover functionality in an application or web form can enable a glossary definition to be shown when cursor is on a field or term.
</p><p>Other examples of business metadata include annotation ability within applications.  For example, a business user may be viewing a <a href="/wiki/Business_intelligence" title="Business intelligence">business intelligence</a> (BI) report and notice a trend in the data.  The user may have background knowledge as to why this trend occurs.  Some business intelligence tools enable the user to create an annotation within the report that explains the trend.  Such an annotation can enhance other users' understanding of the data.  This example is especially powerful because it is created by a business user for the use of other business people.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/NISO" class="mw-redirect" title="NISO">NISO</a> distinguishes three types of metadata: descriptive, structural, and administrative.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NISO&#95;9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NISO-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i>Descriptive metadata</i> is typically used for discovery and identification, as information to search and locate an object, such as title, authors, subjects, keywords, and publisher. <i>Structural metadata</i> describes how the components of an object are organized. An example of structural metadata would be how pages are ordered to form chapters of a book. Finally, <i>administrative metadata</i> gives information to help manage the source. Administrative metadata refers to the technical information, such as file type, or when and how the file was created. Two sub-types of administrative metadata are rights management metadata and preservation metadata. <i>Rights management metadata</i> explains <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_Property_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Intellectual Property Rights">intellectual property rights</a>, while <i>preservation metadata</i> contains information to preserve and save a resource.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Understanding&#95;Metadata&#95;10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Understanding_Metadata-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Statistical data repositories have their own requirements for metadata in order to describe not only the source and quality of the data<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:4&#95;5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but also what statistical processes were used to create the data, which is of particular importance to the statistical community in order to both validate and improve the process of statistical data production.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:5&#95;6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>An additional type of metadata beginning to be more developed is <i>accessibility metadata</i>. Accessibility metadata is not a new concept to libraries; however, advances in universal design have raised its profile.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Beyene&#95;(2017)&#95;11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beyene_(2017)-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 213–214">&#58;&#8202;213–214&#8202;</span></sup> Projects like Cloud4All and GPII identified the lack of common terminologies and models to describe the needs and preferences of users and information that fits those needs as a major gap in providing universal access solutions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Beyene&#95;(2017)&#95;11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beyene_(2017)-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 210–211">&#58;&#8202;210–211&#8202;</span></sup> Those types of information are accessibility metadata.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Beyene&#95;(2017)&#95;11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beyene_(2017)-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 214">&#58;&#8202;214&#8202;</span></sup> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://schema.org/">Schema.org</a> has incorporated several accessibility properties based on IMS Global Access for All Information Model Data Element Specification.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Beyene&#95;(2017)&#95;11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beyene_(2017)-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 214">&#58;&#8202;214&#8202;</span></sup> The Wiki page <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.w3.org/wiki/WebSchemas/Accessibility">WebSchemas/Accessibility</a> lists several properties and their values.  While the efforts to describe and standardize the varied accessibility needs of information seekers are beginning to become more robust, their adoption into established metadata schemas has not been as developed. For example, while Dublin Core (DC)'s "audience" and MARC 21's "reading level" could be used to identify resources suitable for users with dyslexia and DC's "format" could be used to identify resources available in braille, audio, or large print formats, there is more work to be done.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Beyene&#95;(2017)&#95;11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beyene_(2017)-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 214">&#58;&#8202;214&#8202;</span></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Metadata has various purposes. It can help users <a href="/wiki/Findability" title="Findability">find relevant information</a> and <a href="/wiki/Discoverability" title="Discoverability">discover resources</a>. It can also help organize electronic resources, provide digital identification, and archive and preserve resources. Metadata allows users to access resources by "allowing resources to be found by relevant criteria, identifying resources, bringing similar resources together, distinguishing dissimilar resources, and giving location information".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Understanding&#95;Metadata&#95;10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Understanding_Metadata-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Metadata of <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" title="Telecommunications">telecommunication</a> activities including <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> traffic is very widely collected by various national governmental organizations. This data is used for the purposes of <a href="/wiki/Traffic_analysis" title="Traffic analysis">traffic analysis</a> and can be used for <a href="/wiki/Mass_surveillance" title="Mass surveillance">mass surveillance</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Metadata was traditionally used in the <a href="/wiki/Library_catalog" title="Library catalog">card catalogs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Library" title="Library">libraries</a> until the 1980s when libraries converted their catalog data to digital <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">databases</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the 2000s, as data and information were increasingly stored digitally, this digital data was described using <a href="/wiki/Metadata_standards" class="mw-redirect" title="Metadata standards">metadata standards</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>An early description of "meta data" for computer systems was written by David Griffel and Stuart McIntosh at the <a href="/wiki/MIT_Center_for_International_Studies" title="MIT Center for International Studies">MIT Center for International Studies</a>  in 1967:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> "In summary then, we have statements in an object language about subject descriptions of data and token codes for the data. We also have statements in a meta language describing the data relationships and transformations, and ought/is relations between norm and data."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Unique metadata standards exist for different disciplines (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Museum" title="Museum">museum</a> collections, <a href="/wiki/Digital_audio_file" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital audio file">digital audio files</a>, <a href="/wiki/Website" title="Website">websites</a>, etc.). Describing the <a href="/wiki/Content_(media)" class="mw-redirect" title="Content (media)">contents</a> and <a href="/wiki/Context_(computing)" title="Context (computing)">context</a> of data or <a href="/wiki/Computer_file" title="Computer file">data files</a> increases its usefulness. For example, a <a href="/wiki/HTML_editor" title="HTML editor">web page</a> may include metadata specifying what software language the page is written in (e.g., HTML), what tools were used to create it, what subjects the page is about, and where to find more information about the subject. This metadata can automatically improve the reader's experience and make it easier for users to find the web page online.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Practices&#95;in&#95;Using&#95;Metadata&#95;17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Practices_in_Using_Metadata-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/CD" class="mw-redirect" title="CD">CD</a> may include metadata providing information about the musicians, singers, and songwriters whose work appears on the disc.
</p><p>In many countries, government organizations routinely store metadata about emails, telephone calls, web pages, video traffic, IP connections, and cell phone locations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Definition">Definition</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Definition"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Metadata means "data about data". Metadata is defined as the data providing information about one or more aspects of the data; it is used to summarize basic information about data that can make tracking and working with specific data easier.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some examples include:
</p>
<ul><li>Means of creation of the data</li>
<li>Source of the data</li>
<li>Time and date of creation</li>
<li>Creator or author of the data</li>
<li>Location on a <a href="/wiki/Computer_network" title="Computer network">computer network</a> where the data was created</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Technical_standard" title="Technical standard">Standards</a> used</li>
<li>Data quality</li></ul>
<p>For example, a <a href="/wiki/Digital_image" title="Digital image">digital image</a> may include metadata that describes the size of the image, its color depth, resolution, when it was created, the shutter speed, and other data.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A text document's metadata may contain information about how long the document is, who the author is, when the document was written, and a short summary of the document. Metadata within web pages can also contain descriptions of page content, as well as key words linked to the content.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Rouse,&#95;M&#95;(2014)&#95;21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rouse,_M_(2014)-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These links are often called "<a href="/wiki/Tag_(metadata)" title="Tag (metadata)">Metatags</a>", which were used as the primary factor in determining order for a web search until the late 1990s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Rouse,&#95;M&#95;(2014)&#95;21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rouse,_M_(2014)-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The reliance on metatags in web searches was decreased in the late 1990s because of "keyword stuffing",<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Rouse,&#95;M&#95;(2014)&#95;21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rouse,_M_(2014)-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> whereby metatags were being largely misused to trick search engines into thinking some websites had more relevance in the search than they really did.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Rouse,&#95;M&#95;(2014)&#95;21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rouse,_M_(2014)-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Metadata can be stored and managed in a <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">database</a>, often called a <a href="/wiki/Metadata_registry" title="Metadata registry">metadata registry</a> or <a href="/wiki/Metadata_repository" title="Metadata repository">metadata repository</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, without context and a point of reference, it might be impossible to identify metadata just by looking at it.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For example: by itself, a database containing several numbers, all 13 digits long could be the results of calculations or a list of numbers to plug into an <span class="nowrap">equation&#8202;&#160;&#8211;&#32;</span>&#8202;without any other context, the numbers themselves can be perceived as the data. But if given the context that this database is a log of a book collection, those 13-digit numbers may now be identified as <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/ISBN" title="ISBN">ISBNs</a>&#8202;&#160;&#8211;&#32;</span>&#8202;information that refers to the book, but is not itself the information within the book. The term "metadata" was coined in 1968 by Philip Bagley, in his book "Extension of Programming Language Concepts" where it is clear that he uses the term in the ISO 11179 "traditional" sense, which is "structural metadata" i.e. "data about the containers of data"; rather than the alternative sense "content about individual instances of data content" or metacontent, the type of data usually found in library catalogs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Bagley&#95;24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bagley-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since then the fields of information management, information science, information technology, librarianship, and <a href="/wiki/GIS" class="mw-redirect" title="GIS">GIS</a> have widely adopted the term. In these fields, the word <i>metadata</i> is defined as "data about data".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NISO&#95;9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NISO-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> While this is the generally accepted definition, various disciplines have adopted their own more specific explanations and uses of the term.
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Slate_(magazine)" title="Slate (magazine)">Slate</a></i> reported in 2013 that the United States government's interpretation of "metadata" could be broad, and might include message content such as the subject lines of emails.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Structures">Structures</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Structures"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cenchrus_ciliaris_L._438045083.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Cenchrus_ciliaris_L._438045083.jpg/250px-Cenchrus_ciliaris_L._438045083.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="383" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Cenchrus_ciliaris_L._438045083.jpg/500px-Cenchrus_ciliaris_L._438045083.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="3353" data-file-height="5141" /></a><figcaption>Metadata can come in different layers: This physical <a href="/wiki/Herbarium" title="Herbarium">herbarium</a> record of <i><a href="/wiki/Cenchrus_ciliaris" title="Cenchrus ciliaris">Cenchrus ciliaris</a></i> consists of the specimens as well as metadata about them, while the barcode points to a digital record with metadata about the physical record.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Metadata (metacontent) or, more correctly, the vocabularies used to assemble metadata (metacontent) statements, is typically structured according to a standardized concept using a well-defined metadata scheme, including <a href="/wiki/Metadata_standards" class="mw-redirect" title="Metadata standards">metadata standards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metadata_modeling" title="Metadata modeling">metadata models</a>. Tools such as <a href="/wiki/Controlled_vocabulary" title="Controlled vocabulary">controlled vocabularies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taxonomy_(general)" class="mw-redirect" title="Taxonomy (general)">taxonomies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thesaurus_(information_retrieval)" title="Thesaurus (information retrieval)">thesauri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Data_Dictionary" class="mw-redirect" title="Data Dictionary">data dictionaries</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Metadata_registry" title="Metadata registry">metadata registries</a> can be used to apply further standardization to the metadata. Structural metadata commonality is also of paramount importance in <a href="/wiki/Data_model" title="Data model">data model</a> development and in <a href="/wiki/Database_design" title="Database design">database design</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Syntax">Syntax</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Syntax"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Metadata (metacontent) syntax refers to the rules created to structure the fields or elements of metadata (metacontent).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A single metadata scheme may be expressed in a number of different markup or programming languages, each of which requires a different syntax. For example, Dublin Core may be expressed in plain text, <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a>, <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Resource_Description_Framework" title="Resource Description Framework">RDF</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A common example of (guide) metacontent is the bibliographic classification, the subject, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dewey_Decimal_classes" title="List of Dewey Decimal classes">Dewey Decimal class number</a>. There is always an implied statement in any "classification" of some object. To classify an object as, for example, Dewey class number 514 (Topology) (i.e. books having the number 514 on their spine) the implied statement is: "&lt;book&gt;&lt;subject heading&gt;&lt;514&gt;". This is a subject-predicate-object triple, or more importantly, a class-attribute-value triple. The first 2 elements of the triple (class, attribute) are pieces of some structural metadata having a defined semantic. The third element is a value, preferably from some controlled vocabulary, some reference (master) data. The combination of the metadata and master data elements results in a statement which is a metacontent statement i.e. "metacontent = metadata + master data". All of these elements can be thought of as "vocabulary". Both metadata and master data are vocabularies that can be assembled into metacontent statements. There are many sources of these vocabularies, both meta and master data: UML, EDIFACT, XSD, Dewey/UDC/LoC, SKOS, ISO-25964, Pantone, Linnaean Binomial Nomenclature, etc. Using controlled vocabularies for the components of metacontent statements, whether for indexing or finding, is endorsed by <a href="/wiki/ISO_25964" title="ISO 25964">ISO 25964</a>: "If both the indexer and the searcher are guided to choose the same term for the same concept, then relevant documents will be retrieved."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This is particularly relevant when considering search engines of the internet, such as Google. The process indexes pages and then matches text strings using its complex algorithm; there is no intelligence or "inferencing" occurring, just the illusion thereof.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Hierarchical,_linear,_and_planar_schemata"><span id="Hierarchical.2C_linear.2C_and_planar_schemata"></span>Hierarchical, linear, and planar schemata</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Hierarchical, linear, and planar schemata"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Metadata schemata can be hierarchical in nature where relationships exist between metadata elements and elements are nested so that parent-child relationships exist between the elements.
An example of a hierarchical metadata schema is the <a href="/wiki/Learning_object_metadata" title="Learning object metadata">IEEE LOM</a> schema, in which metadata elements may belong to a parent metadata element.
Metadata schemata can also be one-dimensional, or linear, where each element is completely discrete from other elements and classified according to one dimension only.
An example of a linear metadata schema is the <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Core_Metadata_Initiative" class="mw-redirect" title="Dublin Core Metadata Initiative">Dublin Core</a> schema, which is one-dimensional.
Metadata schemata are often 2 dimensional, or planar, where each element is completely discrete from other elements but classified according to 2 orthogonal dimensions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Granularity">Granularity</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Granularity"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The degree to which the data or metadata is structured is referred to as <a href="/wiki/Data_granularity" class="mw-redirect" title="Data granularity">"granularity"</a>. "Granularity" refers to how much detail is provided. Metadata with a high granularity allows for deeper, more detailed, and more structured information and enables a greater level of technical manipulation. A lower level of granularity means that metadata can be created for considerably lower costs but will not provide as detailed information. The major impact of granularity is not only on creation and capture, but moreover on maintenance costs. As soon as the metadata structures become outdated, so too is the access to the referred data. Hence granularity must take into account the effort to create the metadata as well as the effort to maintain it.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Hypermapping">Hypermapping</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Hypermapping"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In all cases where the metadata schemata exceed the planar depiction, some type of hypermapping is required to enable display and view of metadata according to chosen aspect and to serve special views. Hypermapping frequently applies to layering of geographical and geological information overlays.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Standards">Standards</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Standards"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>International standards apply to metadata. Much work is being accomplished in the national and international standards communities, especially <a href="/wiki/ANSI" class="mw-redirect" title="ANSI">ANSI</a> (American National Standards Institute) and <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Standardization" title="International Organization for Standardization">ISO</a> (International Organization for Standardization) to reach a consensus on standardizing metadata and registries. The core metadata registry standard is <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Standardization" title="International Organization for Standardization">ISO</a>/<a href="/wiki/International_Electrotechnical_Commission" title="International Electrotechnical Commission">IEC</a> 11179 Metadata Registries (MDR), the framework for the standard is described in ISO/IEC 11179-1:2004.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A new edition of Part 1 is in its final stage for publication in 2015 or early 2016. It has been revised to align with the current edition of Part 3, ISO/IEC 11179-3:2013<sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which extends the MDR to support the registration of Concept Systems.
(see <a href="/wiki/ISO/IEC_11179" title="ISO/IEC 11179">ISO/IEC 11179</a>). This standard specifies a schema for recording both the meaning and technical structure of the data for unambiguous usage by humans and computers. ISO/IEC 11179 standard refers to metadata as information objects about data, or "data about data". In ISO/IEC 11179 Part-3, the information objects are data about Data Elements, Value Domains, and other reusable semantic and representational information objects that describe the meaning and technical details of a data item. This standard also prescribes the details for a metadata registry, and for registering and administering the information objects within a Metadata Registry. ISO/IEC 11179 Part 3 also has provisions for describing compound structures that are derivations of other data elements, for example through calculations, collections of one or more data elements, or other forms of derived data. While this standard describes itself originally as a "data element" registry, its purpose is to support describing and registering metadata content independently of any particular application, lending the descriptions to being discovered and reused by humans or computers in developing new applications, databases, or for analysis of data collected in accordance with the registered metadata content. This standard has become the general basis for other kinds of metadata registries, reusing and extending the registration and administration portion of the standard.
</p><p>The Geospatial community has a tradition of specialized <a href="/wiki/Geospatial_metadata" title="Geospatial metadata">geospatial metadata</a> standards, particularly building on traditions of map- and image-libraries and catalogs. Formal metadata is usually essential for geospatial data, as common text-processing approaches are not applicable.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Core" title="Dublin Core">Dublin Core</a> metadata terms are a set of vocabulary terms that can be used to describe resources for the purposes of discovery. The original set of 15 classic<sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> metadata terms, known as the Dublin Core Metadata Element Set<sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are endorsed in the following standards documents:
</p>
<ul><li>IETF RFC 5013<sup id="cite&#95;ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>ISO Standard 15836-2009<sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>NISO Standard Z39.85.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The W3C Data Catalog Vocabulary (DCAT)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is an RDF vocabulary that supplements Dublin Core with classes for Dataset, Data Service, Catalog, and Catalog Record. DCAT also uses elements from FOAF, PROV-O, and OWL-Time. DCAT provides an RDF model to support the typical structure of a catalog that contains records, each describing a dataset or service.
</p><p>
Although not a standard, <a href="/wiki/Microformat" title="Microformat">Microformat</a> (also mentioned in the section <a href="#Internet">metadata on the internet</a> below) is a web-based approach to semantic markup which seeks to re-use existing HTML/XHTML <a href="/wiki/Tag_(metadata)" title="Tag (metadata)">tags</a> to convey metadata. Microformat follows XHTML and HTML standards but is not a standard in itself. One advocate of microformats, <a href="/wiki/Tantek_%C3%87elik" title="Tantek Çelik">Tantek Çelik</a>, characterized a problem with alternative approaches: <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1244412712">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 32px}.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;margin-top:0}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{padding-left:1.6em}}</style></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Here's a new language we want you to learn, and now you need to output these additional files on your server. It's a hassle. (Microformats) lower the barrier to entry.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Wharton000&#95;40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wharton000-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Use">Use</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Use"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In metadata, Naming and Design Rules are a set of guidelines and naming conventions that go beyond what a single data exchange standard specification will permit.  The most common standard that Naming and Design Rules are created on is <a href="/wiki/XML_Schema_(W3C)" title="XML Schema (W3C)">XML Schema</a>.  For example, the use of upper <a href="/wiki/Camel_case" title="Camel case">camel case</a> <a href="/wiki/Data_element" title="Data element">data element</a> names is a convention used in many standard but is not specified by the XML Schema specification. Naming and Design Rules have become an important aspect of each organizations data exchange standards.  Within the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, Naming and Design Rules standards are recommended for each federal and state agency.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="File_metadata">File metadata</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: File metadata"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Libopus_1.5.2_screenshot.webp" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="Example of file metadata of an Opus audio file, using Vorbis comments" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Libopus_1.5.2_screenshot.webp/250px-Libopus_1.5.2_screenshot.webp.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="187" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Libopus_1.5.2_screenshot.webp/500px-Libopus_1.5.2_screenshot.webp.png 1.5x" data-file-width="719" data-file-height="538" /></a><figcaption>Example of file metadata of an <a href="/wiki/Opus_(audio_format)" title="Opus (audio format)">Opus</a> audio file, using <a href="/wiki/Vorbis_comment" title="Vorbis comment">Vorbis comment</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Most common types of <a href="/wiki/Computer_file" title="Computer file">computer files</a> can embed metadata, including documents, (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office" title="Microsoft Office">Microsoft Office</a> files, <a href="/wiki/OpenDocument" title="OpenDocument">OpenDocument</a> files, <a href="/wiki/PDF" title="PDF">PDF</a>) images, (e.g. <a href="/wiki/JPEG" title="JPEG">JPEG</a>, <a href="/wiki/PNG" title="PNG">PNG</a>) Video files, (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Audio_Video_Interleave" title="Audio Video Interleave">AVI</a>, <a href="/wiki/MP4" class="mw-redirect" title="MP4">MP4</a>) and audio files. (e.g. <a href="/wiki/WAV" title="WAV">WAV</a>, <a href="/wiki/MP3" title="MP3">MP3</a>)
</p><p>Metadata may be added to files by users, but some metadata is often automatically added to files by authoring applications or by devices used to produce the files, without user intervention. 
</p><p>While metadata in files are useful for finding them, they can be a <a href="/wiki/Privacy" title="Privacy">privacy</a> hazard when the files are shared. Using <a href="/wiki/Metadata_removal_tool" title="Metadata removal tool">metadata removal tools</a> to clean files before sharing them can mitigate this risk.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Photographs">Photographs</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Photographs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Metadata may be written into a <a href="/wiki/Digital_photo" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital photo">digital photo</a> file that will identify who owns it, copyright and contact information, what brand or model of camera created the file, along with exposure information (shutter speed, f-stop, etc.) and descriptive information, such as keywords about the photo, making the file or image searchable on a computer and/or the Internet. Some metadata is created by the camera such as, color space, color channels, exposure time, and aperture (EXIF), while some is input by the photographer and/or software after downloading to a computer.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Most digital cameras write metadata about the model number, shutter speed, etc., and some enable you to edit it;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> this functionality has been available on most Nikon DSLRs since the <a href="/wiki/Nikon_D3" title="Nikon D3">Nikon D3</a>, on most new Canon cameras since the <a href="/wiki/Canon_EOS_7D" title="Canon EOS 7D">Canon EOS 7D</a>, and on most Pentax DSLRs since the Pentax K-3. Metadata can be used to make organizing in post-production easier with the use of key-wording. Filters can be used to analyze a specific set of photographs and create selections on criteria like rating or capture time. On devices with geolocation capabilities like <a href="/wiki/Global_Positioning_System" title="Global Positioning System">GPS</a> (smartphones in particular), the location the photo was taken from may also be included.
</p><p>Photographic Metadata Standards are governed by organizations that develop the following standards. They include, but are not limited to:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/IPTC_Information_Interchange_Model" title="IPTC Information Interchange Model">IPTC Information Interchange Model</a> IIM (International Press Telecommunications Council)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_Press_Telecommunications_Council" title="International Press Telecommunications Council">IPTC</a> Core Schema for XMP</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Extensible_Metadata_Platform" title="Extensible Metadata Platform">XMP</a> – Extensible Metadata Platform (an ISO standard)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Exchangeable_image_file_format" class="mw-redirect" title="Exchangeable image file format">Exif</a> – Exchangeable image file format, Maintained by CIPA (Camera &amp; Imaging Products Association) and published by JEITA (Japan Electronics and Information Technology Industries Association)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dublin_Core" title="Dublin Core">Dublin Core</a> (Dublin Core Metadata Initiative – DCMI)</li>
<li>PLUS (Picture Licensing Universal System)</li>
<li>VRA Core (Visual Resource Association)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JPEG" title="JPEG">JPEG</a> or JPG  is a joint Photographic Experts Group</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Video">Video</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Video"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Metadata is particularly useful in video, where information about its contents (such as transcripts of conversations and text descriptions of its scenes) is not directly understandable by a computer, but where an efficient search of the content is desirable. This is particularly useful in video applications such as <a href="/wiki/Automatic_number-plate_recognition" title="Automatic number-plate recognition">Automatic Number Plate Recognition</a> and Vehicle Recognition Identification software, wherein license plate data is saved and used to create reports and alerts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are 2 sources in which video metadata is derived: (1) operational gathered metadata, that is information about the content produced, such as the type of equipment, software, date, and location; (2) human-authored metadata, to improve search engine visibility, discoverability, audience engagement, and providing advertising opportunities to video publishers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Avid's MetaSync and Adobe's Bridge are examples of professional video editing software with access to metadata.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Telecommunications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Information on the times, origins and destinations of phone calls, electronic messages, instant messages, and other modes of telecommunication, as opposed to message content, is another form of metadata. Bulk collection of this <a href="/wiki/Call_detail_record" title="Call detail record">call detail record</a> metadata by intelligence agencies has proven controversial after disclosures by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Snowden" title="Edward Snowden">Edward Snowden</a> of the fact that certain Intelligence agencies such as the <a href="/wiki/NSA" class="mw-redirect" title="NSA">NSA</a> had been (and perhaps still are) keeping online metadata on millions of internet users for up to a year, regardless of whether or not they [ever] were persons of interest to the agency.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Geospatial_metadata">Geospatial metadata</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Geospatial metadata"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geospatial_metadata" title="Geospatial metadata">Geospatial metadata</a></div>
<p>Geospatial metadata relates to Geographic Information Systems (GIS) files, maps, images, and other data that is location-based. Metadata is used in GIS to document the characteristics and attributes of geographic data, such as database files and data that is developed within a GIS. It includes details like who developed the data, when it was collected, how it was processed, and what formats it's available in, and then delivers the context for the data to be used effectively.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Creation">Creation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Creation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sphagnum_papillosum_at_Sphagnum_cultivation_at_Universit%C3%A4t_Greifswald_2023-06-11_01.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Sphagnum_papillosum_at_Sphagnum_cultivation_at_Universit%C3%A4t_Greifswald_2023-06-11_01.jpg/250px-Sphagnum_papillosum_at_Sphagnum_cultivation_at_Universit%C3%A4t_Greifswald_2023-06-11_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Sphagnum_papillosum_at_Sphagnum_cultivation_at_Universit%C3%A4t_Greifswald_2023-06-11_01.jpg/500px-Sphagnum_papillosum_at_Sphagnum_cultivation_at_Universit%C3%A4t_Greifswald_2023-06-11_01.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="8384" data-file-height="5612" /></a><figcaption>Manually created metadata, in this case for a <i><a href="/wiki/Sphagnum_papillosum" title="Sphagnum papillosum">Sphagnum papillosum</a></i> pot that is part of a <a href="/wiki/Common_garden_experiment" class="mw-redirect" title="Common garden experiment">common garden experiment</a> at <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A4t_Greifswald" class="mw-redirect" title="Universität Greifswald">Universität Greifswald</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Metadata can be created either by automated information processing or by manual work. Elementary metadata captured by computers can include information about when an object was created, who created it, when it was last updated, file size, and file extension. In this context an <i>object</i> refers to any of the following:
</p>
<ul><li>A physical item such as a book, CD, DVD, a paper map, chair, table, flower pot, etc.</li>
<li>An electronic file such as a digital image, digital photo, electronic document, program file, database table, etc.</li></ul>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Metadata_engine" title="Metadata engine">metadata engine</a> collects, stores and analyzes information about data and metadata in use within a domain.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Data_virtualization">Data virtualization</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Data virtualization"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Data_virtualization" title="Data virtualization">Data virtualization</a></div>
<p>Data virtualization emerged in the 2000s as the new software technology to complete the virtualization "stack" in the enterprise. Metadata is used in data virtualization servers which are enterprise infrastructure components, alongside database and application servers. Metadata in these servers is saved as persistent repository and describe <a href="/wiki/Business_object" title="Business object">business objects</a> in various enterprise systems and applications. Structural metadata commonality is also important to support data virtualization.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Statistics_and_census_services">Statistics and census services</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Statistics and census services"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Standardization and harmonization work has brought advantages to industry efforts to build metadata systems in the statistical community.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-GløersenImprov11&#95;50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GløersenImprov11-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-LaurilaMetadata12&#95;51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LaurilaMetadata12-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Several metadata guidelines and standards such as the European Statistics Code of Practice<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ECEuropeanStat&#95;52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECEuropeanStat-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and ISO 17369:2013 (<a href="/wiki/SDMX" title="SDMX">Statistical Data and Metadata Exchange</a> or SDMX)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-GløersenImprov11&#95;50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GløersenImprov11-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> provide key principles for how businesses, government bodies, and other entities should manage statistical data and metadata. Entities such as <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-UNReportOn15&#95;53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNReportOn15-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/European_System_of_Central_Banks" title="European System of Central Banks">European System of Central Banks</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-UNReportOn15&#95;53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNReportOn15-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">U.S. Environmental Protection Agency</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-EPAMetadata17&#95;54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPAMetadata17-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> have implemented these and other such standards and guidelines with the goal of improving "efficiency when managing statistical business processes".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-UNReportOn15&#95;53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNReportOn15-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Library_and_information_science">Library and information science</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Library and information science"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

<div class="sidebar-list mw-collapsible mw-collapsed"><div class="sidebar-list-title" style="background:#ddddff; text-align:center;;color: var(--color-base)">Areas</div><div class="sidebar-list-content mw-collapsible-content"><a href="/wiki/Academic_library" title="Academic library">Academic</a> - <a href="/wiki/Archive" title="Archive">Archival</a> - <a href="/wiki/Law_library" title="Law library">Legal</a> - <a href="/wiki/Medical_library" title="Medical library">Health</a> - <a href="/wiki/Private_library" title="Private library">Private</a> - <a href="/wiki/Public_library" title="Public library">Public</a> - <a href="/wiki/School_library" title="School library">School</a> - <a href="/wiki/Special_library" title="Special library">Special</a></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-below" style="border-top:1px solid #aaa;border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Libraries" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Libraries">WikiProject</a></li>
<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="noviewer" typeof="mw:File"><span title="Category"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/Symbol_category_class.svg/20px-Symbol_category_class.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" class="mw-file-element" href="/wiki/Category:Library_and_information_science" title="Category:Library and information science">Category</a></span></li></ul></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333133064" /><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1239400231">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}html.skin-theme-clientpref-night .mw-parser-output .navbar li a abbr{color:var(--color-base)!important}@media(prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .navbar li a abbr{color:var(--color-base)!important}}@media print{.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:none!important}}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:LibraryandInformation-TopicSidebar" title="Template:LibraryandInformation-TopicSidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:LibraryandInformation-TopicSidebar" title="Template talk:LibraryandInformation-TopicSidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:LibraryandInformation-TopicSidebar" title="Special:EditPage/Template:LibraryandInformation-TopicSidebar"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Metadata has been used in various ways as a means of cataloging items in libraries in both digital and analog formats. Such data helps classify, aggregate, identify, and locate a particular book, DVD, magazine, or any object a library might hold in its collection.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Until the 1980s, many library catalogs used 3x5 inch cards in file drawers to display a book's title, author, subject matter, and an abbreviated <a href="/wiki/Alphanumeric" class="mw-redirect" title="Alphanumeric">alpha-numeric</a> string (<a href="/wiki/Call_number" class="mw-redirect" title="Call number">call number</a>) which indicated the physical location of the book within the library's shelves. The <a href="/wiki/Dewey_Decimal_Classification" title="Dewey Decimal Classification">Dewey Decimal System</a> employed by libraries for the classification of library materials by subject is an early example of metadata usage. The early paper catalog had information regarding whichever item was described on said card: title, author, subject, and a number as to where to find said item.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Beginning in the 1980s and 1990s, many libraries replaced these paper file cards with computer databases. These computer databases make it much easier and faster for users to do keyword searches. Another form of older metadata collection is the use by the US Census Bureau of what is known as the "Long Form". The Long Form asks questions that are used to create demographic data to find patterns of distribution.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Library" title="Library">Libraries</a> employ metadata in <a href="/wiki/Library_catalog" title="Library catalog">library catalogues</a>, most commonly as part of an <a href="/wiki/Library_management_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Library management system">Integrated Library Management System</a>. Metadata is obtained by <a href="/wiki/Library_cataloging#Cataloging_rules" class="mw-redirect" title="Library cataloging">cataloging</a> resources such as books, periodicals, DVDs, web pages or digital images. This data is stored in the integrated library management system, <a href="/wiki/Library_management_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Library management system">ILMS</a>, using the <a href="/wiki/MARC_standards" title="MARC standards">MARC</a> metadata standard. The purpose is to direct patrons to the physical or electronic location of items or areas they seek as well as to provide a description of the item/s in question.
</p><p>More recent and specialized instances of library metadata include the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Digital_library" title="Digital library">digital libraries</a> including <a href="/wiki/Eprint" title="Eprint">e-print</a> repositories and digital image libraries. While often based on library principles, the focus on non-librarian use, especially in providing metadata, means they do not follow traditional or common cataloging approaches. Given the custom nature of included materials, metadata fields are often specially created e.g. taxonomic classification fields, location fields, keywords, or copyright statement. Standard file information such as file size and format are usually automatically included.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-solodovnik&#95;58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solodovnik-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Library operation has for decades been a key topic in efforts toward <a href="/wiki/International_standardization" class="mw-redirect" title="International standardization">international standardization</a>. Standards for metadata in digital libraries include <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Core" title="Dublin Core">Dublin Core</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metadata_Encoding_and_Transmission_Standard" title="Metadata Encoding and Transmission Standard">METS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metadata_Object_Description_Schema" title="Metadata Object Description Schema">MODS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Data_Documentation_Initiative" title="Data Documentation Initiative">DDI</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">DOI</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uniform_Resource_Name" title="Uniform Resource Name">URN</a>, <a href="/wiki/Preservation_Metadata:_Implementation_Strategies" title="Preservation Metadata: Implementation Strategies">PREMIS</a> schema, <a href="/wiki/Ecological_Metadata_Language" title="Ecological Metadata Language">EML</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Protocol_for_Metadata_Harvesting" class="mw-redirect" title="Protocol for Metadata Harvesting">OAI-PMH</a>. Leading libraries in the world give hints on their metadata standards strategies.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A similar concept is the synset, short for <i>synonym set</i>, a group of one or more <a href="/wiki/Synonym" title="Synonym">synonyms</a> that share a common meaning in some context. Synsets are a fundamental concept in <a href="/wiki/Computational_linguistics" title="Computational linguistics">computational linguistics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lexical_semantics" title="Lexical semantics">lexical semantics</a>, most notably used in the <a href="/wiki/WordNet" title="WordNet">WordNet</a> lexical database of English.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Miller1990&#95;61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miller1990-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The concept has been extended to other languages and multilingual projects such as <a href="/wiki/EuroWordNet" title="EuroWordNet">EuroWordNet</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BabelNet" title="BabelNet">BabelNet</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NavigliPonzetto12&#95;63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NavigliPonzetto12-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the Global WordNet initiative.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Synsets have been shown to play an important role in some areas of <a href="/wiki/Natural_Language_Processing" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural Language Processing">Natural Language Processing</a>, providing a bridge between lexical items and conceptual meaning, enabling:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Fellbaum1998&#95;65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fellbaum1998-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Science">Science</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Metadata&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Science"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Metascience" title="Metascience">Metascience</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><span><video id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/FREYA-The-power-of-PIDs-V05-1.webm/250px-seek%3D30-FREYA-The-power-of-PIDs-V05-1.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" data-mw-tmh="" class="mw-file-element" width="250" height="141" data-durationhint="217" data-mwtitle="FREYA-The-power-of-PIDs-V05-1.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" resource="/wiki/File:FREYA-The-power-of-PIDs-V05-1.webm"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/a/a9/FREYA-The-power-of-PIDs-V05-1.webm/FREYA-The-power-of-PIDs-V05-1.webm.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-transcodekey="480p.vp9.webm" data-width="854" data-height="480" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/a/a9/FREYA-The-power-of-PIDs-V05-1.webm/FREYA-The-power-of-PIDs-V05-1.webm.1080p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-width="1920" data-height="1080" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/a/a9/FREYA-The-power-of-PIDs-V05-1.webm/FREYA-The-power-of-PIDs-V05-1.webm.144p.mjpeg.mov" type="video/quicktime" data-transcodekey="144p.mjpeg.mov" data-width="256" data-height="144" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/a/a9/FREYA-The-power-of-PIDs-V05-1.webm/FREYA-The-power-of-PIDs-V05-1.webm.240p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-transcodekey="240p.vp9.webm" data-width="426" data-height="240" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/a/a9/FREYA-The-power-of-PIDs-V05-1.webm/FREYA-The-power-of-PIDs-V05-1.webm.360p.webm" type="video/webm;
